Welcome to Rock Solid Troubleshooter

üìñ How to Use This Guide

Organized by SYMPTOM, not by cause.

When you have a problem:

  1. Find the symptom you're observing
  2. Follow the diagnostic steps
  3. Implement the solution
  4. Document what worked

Priority Levels

üî¥ CRITICAL Stop drilling immediately - Safety or equipment at immediate risk
üü° IMPORTANT Address before continuing - Will worsen if not resolved
üü¢ MONITOR Watch closely - May worsen, but not immediately critical

Troubleshooting Philosophy

5-Step Systematic Approach:

  1. Observe first - What exactly is happening?
  2. Think systematically - What could cause this?
  3. Start simple - Check obvious things first
  4. Change one thing - So you know what worked
  5. Document everything - For next time

‚ò†Ô∏è Drilling Problems

üî¥ CRITICAL No Penetration / Zero Advance

Symptom: You're drilling but the hole isn't getting deeper.

Quick Checks (2 minutes):

  • Is bit actually rotating?
  • Is WOB (Weight On Bit) being applied?
  • Is bit on bottom or off bottom?
  • Check depth gauge/measurement
Decision Point:

Is bit rotating?

‚Üí NO: Go to Equipment ‚Üí Rotation Problems

‚Üí YES: Continue with diagnostic steps below

Step 1: Check Bit Loading

1. Pull bit and inspect face

2. Is it covered with formation material?

If YES (Bit is balled/loaded):
  • Clean bit thoroughly with wire brush
  • Increase pump pressure by 15-20%
  • Add surfactant to drilling fluid
  • Reduce WOB by 30%
  • Resume drilling and monitor closely

If NO: Continue to Step 2

Step 2: Check Bit Condition

Inspect:

  • Are diamonds visible and sharp?
  • Is matrix intact (not worn away)?
  • Are waterways clear?
If NO (Bit worn out):

‚Üí Replace bit immediately

‚Üí Document: meters drilled, formation type, hours run

If YES: Continue to Step 3

Step 3: Check Formation

Did you hit a void or cavity?

  • Can you feel bit spinning freely?
  • Did you lose circulation suddenly?
  • Are returns suddenly very clean?
If YES (In void):
  • Pull back 0.5-1.0m above void
  • Add LCM (Lost Circulation Materials) to fluid
  • Try to bridge across void
  • May need casing through void zone
  • Consult supervisor if void is extensive

If NO: Continue to Step 4

Step 4: Check Operating Parameters

  • WOB adequate? If too low ‚Üí Increase gradually
  • RPM in correct range? If too low ‚Üí Increase to proper speed
  • Pump pressure/flow adequate? If inadequate ‚Üí Increase

Rare Causes (If all above checks out):

  • Bit threads backed off (bit detached from string)
  • Extreme hardness change (hit metal? Concrete?)
  • Wrong bit type for formation

Action: Pull string, inspect bit connection and bit face carefully

Prevention:

  • Match bit to formation type
  • Monitor penetration rate constantly
  • Keep drilling fluid properties correct
  • Replace bits before completely worn
  • Apply proper thread compound
  • Torque connections to specification

üî¥ CRITICAL Stuck Pipe / Stuck Drill String

Symptom: Cannot move drill string up or down, or cannot rotate.

üî¥ STOP IMMEDIATELY - DO NOT FORCE

Forcing can twist off the string and make recovery much more difficult and expensive.

Initial Assessment (5 minutes):

Can you rotate at all?

  • YES, some rotation ‚Üí Mechanical sticking
  • NO, zero rotation ‚Üí Severe bind

Can you move up/down at all?

  • YES, slight movement ‚Üí Moderate stick
  • NO, completely frozen ‚Üí Severe stick

Where is stuck point?

  • Note depth carefully
  • Shallow = More options available
  • Deep = More challenging recovery

IMMEDIATE ACTIONS - DO THIS FIRST:

Step 1: Work It Gently (10 minutes)

  • Slight back-and-forth rotation (¬±45¬∞)
  • Light up-and-down movement (6-12 inches)
  • Don't exceed 80% of pull capacity
  • Be patient, don't force
  • May take time to work free

Step 2: Circulate (if possible)

  • Start pump at low pressure
  • Gradually increase flow
  • Fluid may lubricate stuck point
  • Continue gentle working while circulating

Step 3: Rest and Soak (15-60 minutes)

If Steps 1-2 don't work immediately:

  • Leave under light tension
  • Allow fluid to penetrate stuck zone
  • May work free with time
  • Check every 15 minutes

IF STILL STUCK - IDENTIFY TYPE:

Type 1: Differential Sticking

Symptoms:

  • Cannot pull up
  • Some rotation possible
  • Happened when stopped drilling
  • In permeable formation

Cause: Pressure differential presses string against wall like suction cup

Solutions:

  • Reduce mud weight
  • Spot lubricating pill (diesel/oil-based)
  • Allow 4-8 hours soak time
  • Work gently while soaking
  • Jar upward if jar available

Type 2: Mechanical Sticking

Symptoms:

  • Cannot rotate
  • May be able to pull some
  • Associated with ledge or dogleg

Cause: Key seat (narrow spot), borehole irregularity, stabilizer caught

Solutions:

  • Work back and forth
  • Pull and rotate simultaneously
  • May need to back off a joint
  • Possible need for jarring

Type 3: Cuttings Pack-Off

Symptoms:

  • Gradual increase in drag
  • Finally stuck completely
  • Poor hole cleaning was evident

Cause: Cuttings accumulated and bridged across annulus

Solutions:

  • Circulate at high rate
  • Work string while circulating
  • May need spotting fluid (dispersants)
  • Patience required - may take hours

Type 4: Hole Collapse

Symptoms:

  • Sudden stick
  • In unstable formation
  • May hear/feel collapse

Cause: Borehole wall failure, unconsolidated material

Solutions:

  • Very difficult to resolve
  • Work gently - don't make worse
  • Improve mud properties if possible
  • May require jarring
  • Worst case: back off and sidetrack

When to Call for Professional Help:

  • After 4-6 hours of trying with no progress
  • Risk of twisting off string
  • Valuable hole/equipment at stake
  • Beyond your training/experience

Fishing Tools Available:

  • Overshot (latches outside of string)
  • Jar (delivers impact forces)
  • Spotting sub (delivers fluid to stuck point)
  • Back-off tool (unscrews stuck section)

Prevention:

  • Maintain good hole cleaning always
  • Proper mud properties for formation
  • Don't sit still for long periods
  • Work string regularly (rotate/reciprocate)
  • Ream tight spots immediately
  • Trip slowly through problem zones

üü° IMPORTANT Slow Penetration Rate

Symptom: Drilling is advancing, but slower than normal for this formation.

Quick Assessment:

  • What is your current penetration rate? (m/hr or ft/hr)
  • What was it previously in similar formation?
  • When did you notice the decrease?

Step 1: Check Bit Condition (Most Common Cause)

Pull bit and inspect:

  • Diamond exposure (should be visible)
  • Matrix wear (excessive = replace)
  • Gauge wear (bit diameter)
  • Waterway condition (clean vs. eroded)

Worn bit indicators:

  • Diamonds polished smooth
  • Matrix worn below diamond level
  • Bit gauge reduced >1mm
  • Waterways eroded or plugged

Solution: Replace bit. A worn bit costs more in lost time than it saves in bit cost.

Step 2: Check Operating Parameters

Parameter Action
WOB Increase gradually (10-20% increments)
RPM Soft: 400-600 | Med: 600-800 | Hard: 800-1200
Pump Flow Must cool bit and remove cuttings
Pump Pressure Too high = blockage; Too low = inadequate

Step 3: Check Formation Changes

Did the formation change?

  • Review recent core samples
  • Harder rock = naturally slower
  • May need different bit type
  • Check geological logs if available

Typical Penetration Rates (NQ - Reference)

Formation Expected Rate
Soft sedimentary 3-8 m/hr
Medium metamorphic 2-5 m/hr
Hard igneous 1-3 m/hr
Very hard/abrasive 0.5-1.5 m/hr

Prevention:

  • Track penetration rate continuously
  • Replace bits before performance drops significantly
  • Keep detailed bit performance records
  • Maintain optimal fluid properties
  • Match bit selection to formation

üü° IMPORTANT Excessive Torque

Symptom: Torque is higher than normal for current conditions.

Normal Torque Ranges (NQ, rough guide):

  • Soft rock: 500-1500 ft-lbs
  • Medium rock: 1500-3000 ft-lbs
  • Hard rock: 3000-5000 ft-lbs
  • If >150% of normal for formation = PROBLEM

Quick Actions:

  1. Reduce WOB by 30%
  2. Check for blockages
  3. Monitor closely

Diagnostic Steps:

High Torque + No Penetration?

‚Üí Bit Loading/Balling

  • Pull bit and clean thoroughly
  • Increase pump pressure
  • Add surfactant to fluid
  • Modify drilling parameters

High Torque + Normal Penetration?

Check for these issues:

Issue 1: Borehole Deviation/Drag

  • More common in deep holes
  • Does torque ease when pulled back?

Solution:

  • Use more stabilizers
  • Reduce WOB
  • Check BHA alignment
  • Work string regularly

Issue 2: Cuttings Accumulation

  • Poor return quality
  • Muddy, high-solids fluid

Solution:

  1. Pull off bottom
  2. Circulate clean (15-30 min)
  3. Increase pump rate 20%
  4. Resume drilling

Issue 3: Swelling Formation

  • Reactive clays
  • Time-dependent (gets worse)

Solution:

  • Add clay inhibitor
  • Work string frequently
  • May need oil-based mud
  • Trip out if severe

Issue 4: Mechanical Binding

  • Intermittent torque spikes
  • Grinding/catching sounds

Solution:

  1. Pull string
  2. Inspect for bent rods or damaged BHA
  3. Replace damaged components

üü¢ MONITOR Bit Balling / Loading

Symptom: Cuttings and formation material pack into bit face, reducing or stopping penetration.

Recognition:

  • Sudden decrease in penetration
  • Torque may increase
  • Bit feels like grinding on itself
  • Common in clay-rich formations

Immediate Solutions:

  1. Pull bit immediately
  2. Clean thoroughly with wire brush and water
  3. Inspect waterways - ensure clear
  4. Modify drilling fluid:
    • Add surfactant (reduces sticking)
    • Increase water content (thinner mud)
    • Add dispersants if clay is issue
  5. Reduce WOB by 30-40%
  6. Increase pump pressure 15-20%
  7. Resume drilling - monitor closely

Long-term Prevention:

  • Maintain proper fluid properties
  • Use anti-balling agents in sticky formations
  • Optimal pump flow and pressure
  • Match bit design to formation
  • Avoid excessive WOB

üîß CRITICAL SKILL Bit Dressing & Sharpening Techniques

Purpose: Restore bit cutting ability and extend bit life through proper dressing techniques.

When to Dress a Bit:

  • Penetration rate drops by 30-50% compared to fresh bit
  • Matrix is glazed over (diamonds covered)
  • Waterways becoming restricted
  • Torque increasing without depth gain
  • Every 50-100 meters in abrasive formations

üî© The 3/4" Nut Dressing Method (Field Proven)

This is the most common field technique used by experienced drillers:

Setup:

  1. Materials needed:
    • 3/4" steel nuts (hex nuts, Grade 5 or 8)
    • 2-4 nuts for most bit sizes
    • Clean water supply
    • Wire brush
  2. Pull bit to surface
  3. Clean bit thoroughly:
    • Wire brush face and waterways
    • Remove all cuttings and mud
    • Inspect for damage
  4. Drop nuts into hole:
    • NQ bit: 2-3 nuts
    • HQ bit: 3-4 nuts
    • PQ bit: 4-5 nuts

The Dressing Procedure:

‚ö†Ô∏è CRITICAL PARAMETERS - READ CAREFULLY

Rotation Speed: 3rd Gear (Slow Speed)

  • Typical: 300-500 RPM depending on rig
  • NEVER use high speed - will overheat diamonds
  • Too fast = glazing instead of dressing

Water Flow: CRITICAL

  • Run pump at 50-75% of normal drilling pressure
  • Water must flow continuously during dressing
  • Cools diamonds and flushes away matrix
  • Never dress dry - destroys bit

Pressure/Weight: Light Touch

  • Use 10-20% of normal drilling weight
  • Just enough to keep nuts engaged
  • Let the nuts do the work
  1. Lower bit onto nuts:
    • Start rotation in 3rd gear (slow)
    • Start water pump (50-75% pressure)
    • Gently lower bit onto nuts
    • You'll feel slight resistance when engaged
  2. Dressing action:
    • Keep rotation slow and steady
    • Apply light pressure (1000-2000 lbs)
    • Work in short intervals: 30 seconds on, 30 seconds off
    • Total dressing time: 3-8 minutes
  3. Monitor the process:
    • Listen for grinding sound (good - nuts working)
    • Watch returns - should see fine metal particles
    • Feel for smooth, even resistance
    • No chattering or grabbing (reduce weight if this occurs)

üìä Reading Head Pressure - The Key Indicator

This is how you know when your bit is sharp:

Pressure Gauge Reading Technique:

Before Dressing (Dull Bit):

  • Baseline pressure: Note normal circulation pressure
  • On-bottom pressure: Higher due to restricted waterways
  • Example: Circulating = 300 PSI, On bottom = 450 PSI
  • Difference of 150 PSI indicates dull/loaded bit

During Dressing:

  • Watch pressure gauge continuously
  • Pressure should gradually decrease
  • Indicates waterways opening up
  • Matrix being removed to expose diamonds

After Dressing (Sharp Bit):

  • Circulating pressure: Same as before (300 PSI)
  • On-bottom pressure: Much closer to circulating pressure
  • Example: Circulating = 300 PSI, On bottom = 320-340 PSI
  • Difference of 20-40 PSI = properly dressed bit
  • Target: Less than 50 PSI difference

‚ö†Ô∏è Pressure Reading Rules:

  • If difference exceeds 100 PSI after dressing ‚Üí dress more
  • If difference is less than 20 PSI ‚Üí bit may be overdressed
  • Sudden pressure spike ‚Üí nut jammed, pull up immediately
  • Pressure dropping too fast ‚Üí reducing weight, check for damage

üî¨ Engineering Standards & Bit Profile

Proper Bit Face Geometry:

Crown Profile (What you're trying to achieve):

  • Center Crown: Should be highest point (reference)
  • Inner Gauge: 0.010" - 0.020" below crown
  • Outer Gauge: 0.020" - 0.030" below crown
  • Outside Edge: Should be sharp, not rounded

Diamond Exposure (Critical):

  • Diamonds should protrude 0.005" - 0.015" from matrix
  • Too little exposure = no cutting action
  • Too much exposure = diamonds fall out
  • Use magnifying glass to inspect

Waterway Clearance:

  • All waterways must be clear and open
  • Check with wire or small rod
  • Blockage = immediate overheating
  • Minimum depth: 1/4" into bit body
BIT FACE PROFILE (Side View):
                            
    Crown (highest)    ‚Üë
         __            |  0.010" - 0.020" drop
    Inner |__          |
         Outer |__     ‚Üì  0.020" - 0.030" total
              Edge (sharp)
                            
    = Optimal cutting geometry
    = Even wear distribution
    = Maximum ROP (Rate of Penetration)

‚öôÔ∏è Alternative Dressing Methods

Method When to Use Pros/Cons
3/4" Nuts Standard method, most formations ‚úÖ Cheap, effective, repeatable
‚úÖ Easy to control
‚ö†Ô∏è Requires multiple nuts
Hard Formation Drill in very hard rock (quartzite, granite) ‚úÖ Natural and aggressive
‚úÖ No extra materials
‚ö†Ô∏è Slow process (may take hours)
Grinding Wheel Shop/maintenance facility ‚úÖ Precise control
‚úÖ Can reshape profile
‚ùå Requires special equipment
‚ùå Risk of overheating
Carbide/Corundum Field alternative ‚úÖ Faster than nuts
‚ö†Ô∏è More expensive
‚ö†Ô∏è Can be aggressive
Concrete Block Emergency field method ‚úÖ Usually available
‚ö†Ô∏è Less controlled
‚ö†Ô∏è Messy

üìã Step-by-Step Dressing Checklist

‚úÖ Pre-Dressing Checklist:

  • Record current depth and bit hours
  • Note head pressure before pulling bit
  • Pull bit to surface safely
  • Clean bit thoroughly with wire brush
  • Inspect for cracks, missing diamonds, damage
  • Check waterways are clear
  • Select appropriate dressing materials (nuts or alternative)
  • Verify water pump is operational
  • Set rotation to 3rd gear (slow speed)

‚úÖ During Dressing:

  • Start water flow BEFORE engaging bit
  • Lower bit slowly onto dressing material
  • Apply light pressure (10-20% of drilling weight)
  • Maintain slow, steady rotation
  • Work in intervals: 30 sec on, 30 sec off
  • Watch pressure gauge continuously
  • Listen for smooth grinding sound
  • Check returns for metal particles (good sign)
  • Total time: 3-8 minutes typically

‚úÖ Post-Dressing:

  • Pull bit and inspect face
  • Verify diamonds are exposed (use magnifying glass)
  • Check waterways are clear
  • Look for even wear pattern across face
  • Measure crown profile if possible
  • Clean bit thoroughly again
  • Run to bottom and check penetration rate
  • Record new head pressure on bottom
  • Compare to target (< 50 PSI difference)
  • Document dressing in drill log

‚ö†Ô∏è Common Mistakes & How to Avoid Them

üî¥ CRITICAL ERRORS (Never Do These):

1. Dressing Without Water:

  • ‚ùå NEVER dress a bit dry
  • Friction heat will burn diamonds
  • Glazes matrix instead of removing it
  • Can crack bit body from thermal stress
  • ‚úÖ Always run water at 50-75% pressure

2. Using High Speed:

  • ‚ùå Never use 4th or 5th gear for dressing
  • High speed generates excessive heat
  • Polishes matrix instead of abrading it
  • Can shatter diamonds from heat stress
  • ‚úÖ Always use 3rd gear (slow rotation, 300-500 RPM)

3. Excessive Pressure/Weight:

  • ‚ùå Don't use normal drilling weight
  • Can embed nuts in bit face
  • Can knock diamonds out
  • Can damage bit structure
  • ‚úÖ Use only 10-20% of drilling weight (light touch)

4. Over-Dressing:

  • ‚ùå Don't dress for more than 8-10 minutes
  • Removes too much matrix
  • Diamonds fall out prematurely
  • Shortens bit life
  • ‚úÖ Stop when pressure difference is < 50 PSI

5. Dressing Too Frequently:

  • ‚ùå Don't dress every trip
  • Wastes time and reduces bit life
  • Let bit self-dress in formation when possible
  • ‚úÖ Only dress when penetration drops 30-50%

üéØ Field Tips from Experienced Drillers

üí° Pro Tips:

Tip 1: The Sound Test

  • Sharp bit: Clean, high-pitched cutting sound
  • Dull bit: Grinding, laboring sound
  • Learn to recognize the difference

Tip 2: The Water Test

  • Pull bit, run water through waterways
  • Sharp bit: Strong, even streams from all waterways
  • Dull bit: Weak or blocked waterways
  • If blocked, use wire to clear before dressing

Tip 3: The Formation Trick

  • If you hit very hard formation (quartzite, granite)
  • Let it naturally dress your bit for 1-2 meters
  • Often more effective than mechanical dressing
  • Monitor pressure to avoid overdressing

Tip 4: Nut Selection

  • Use Grade 5 or Grade 8 nuts (harder steel)
  • Grade 2 nuts are too soft - wear out quickly
  • Keep a supply of 3/4" nuts on site
  • Can reuse nuts 2-3 times if not too worn

Tip 5: Timing Dressing

  • Best time: Before shift change (next crew gets sharp bit)
  • Worst time: End of day (rushed work = poor results)
  • Plan ahead - don't wait until bit is completely dead

Tip 6: Record Keeping

  • Keep log of: Bit type, hours run, meters drilled, formations
  • Note pressure readings before/after dressing
  • Track dressing frequency for each bit
  • Helps predict when to dress next bit

Tip 7: Emergency Field Dressing

  • If no nuts available: Use broken concrete or hard rock pieces
  • If no water pump: Gravity feed water down hole while rotating slowly
  • Better to improvise than continue with dead bit
  • But always safer to use proper method when possible

üìä Bit Life Optimization Table

Formation Type Dressing Frequency Expected Bit Life Notes
Soft Sedimentary Every 150-200m 500-800m total Self-dresses well, minimal dressing needed
Medium Hard Every 75-100m 300-500m total Regular dressing extends life significantly
Hard Abrasive Every 50-75m 200-300m total Frequent dressing critical
Very Hard Self-dressing 100-200m total Formation dresses bit naturally
Sticky Clay Every 25-50m Variable Loads quickly, clean frequently

‚ö†Ô∏è When NOT to Dress a Bit:

  • Bit has visible cracks or structural damage ‚Üí Replace immediately
  • More than 50% of diamonds are missing ‚Üí Bit is done
  • Matrix is worn below diamond layer ‚Üí No dressing will help
  • Waterways are severely eroded ‚Üí Safety issue, replace bit
  • Bit has been dressed 5+ times already ‚Üí Diminishing returns
  • In very sticky formation ‚Üí Fix fluid properties first

Remember: Sometimes the right decision is to replace the bit, not dress it. Don't try to squeeze the last meter out of a dead bit - you'll waste more time than the bit is worth.

üíß Fluid System Problems

üî¥ CRITICAL Lost Circulation / No Returns

Symptom: Drilling fluid not returning to surface, or returns much less than pumped.

STOP DRILLING IMMEDIATELY

Continuing can:

  • Collapse the borehole
  • Stick the drill string
  • Waste expensive drilling fluid
  • Cause environmental issues

Quick Assessment:

  • Partial loss: Some returns (50-90%)
  • Severe loss: Minimal returns (10-50%)
  • Total loss: Zero returns (0%)

Common Causes:

  1. Natural Fractures: Fluid escaping into fractures/faults
  2. Cavernous Formation: Large voids in rock (limestone common)
  3. Unconsolidated Zone: Highly permeable sand/gravel
  4. Induced Fractures: Fluid pressure too high, broke formation

IMMEDIATE ACTIONS:

Step 1: Stop and Assess (First 5 minutes)

  1. Stop pumping immediately
  2. Raise bit off bottom 1-2 meters
  3. Monitor fluid pit level
  4. Note exact depth where loss occurred
  5. Assess severity (partial/severe/total)

Step 2: For Partial Loss (50-90% returns)

  1. Reduce pump pressure by 30%
  2. Slow pump rate
  3. Add fine LCM (sawdust, mica, cellophane)
  4. Continue drilling slowly
  5. Monitor - if worsens, move to Step 3

Step 3: For Severe/Total Loss

  1. Pull bit above loss zone
  2. Mix heavy LCM pill:
    • Coarse materials (nutshells, sawdust)
    • Medium materials (mica, cellophane)
    • Fine materials (bentonite, cement)
    • Typical: 5-10 bags per m¬≥ water
  3. Pump LCM pill to loss zone
  4. Leave to set (2-8 hours)
  5. Test by resuming circulation slowly
  6. If successful, ream through zone carefully
  7. If unsuccessful, repeat with different LCM mix or consider cement plug

LCM Materials Guide:

Material Size Best For
Sawdust Fine-Medium Small fractures
Nutshells Coarse Large fractures
Mica Fine Sealing fractures
Cellophane Medium General purpose
Bentonite Very fine Sealing, thickening
Cement Fine Permanent sealing

When to Consider Casing:

  • LCM treatments repeatedly fail
  • Loss zone is extensive (>10m thick)
  • Total loss with no recovery possible
  • Critical to complete the hole

Prevention:

  • Monitor pump pressure constantly
  • Don't over-pressurize weak formations
  • Have LCM pre-mixed and ready
  • Know geology ahead of time
  • Reduce mud weight in fractured zones

üü° IMPORTANT High Pump Pressure

Symptom: Pump pressure higher than normal for current depth and flow rate.

Common Causes:

1. Bit Nozzles Plugged

Symptoms:

  • Sudden pressure increase
  • Penetration rate drops

Solution:

  1. Pull bit to surface
  2. Clean nozzles/waterways thoroughly
  3. Check for debris in fluid system
  4. Improve solids control

2. Fluid Too Viscous (Thick)

Symptoms:

  • Gradual pressure increase
  • Fluid looks very thick/gel-like

Solution:

  1. Dilute with water
  2. Add thinning agents
  3. Increase temperature if cold

3. Packoff / Bridging Downhole

Symptoms:

  • Pressure increases over time
  • May have torque increase
  • Returns quality poor

Solution:

  1. Pull off bottom
  2. Work string up/down
  3. Circulate at high rate
  4. May need to trip out and clean hole

4. Pump Valve Problems

Symptoms:

  • Erratic pressure
  • Pump sounds rough

Solution:

  1. Stop and inspect pump
  2. Check valves and pistons
  3. Replace worn components

Quick Diagnostic Test:

  1. Pull bit off bottom
  2. Check pressure with string open
  3. If pressure drops significantly ‚Üí Problem is at bit or downhole
  4. If pressure stays high ‚Üí Problem is in string or pump

üü° IMPORTANT Poor Fluid Returns

Symptom: Returns to surface but dirty, full of cuttings, or inadequate volume.

Possible Causes & Solutions:

  1. Inadequate Pump Flow
    • Solution: Increase pump speed/pressure
    • Should see clear returns with minimal cuttings
  2. Poor Hole Cleaning
    • Solution: Pull off bottom and circulate for 15-30 min
    • Add dispersants to fluid
    • Work string while circulating
  3. Drilling Too Fast
    • Solution: Reduce penetration rate
    • Allow more time for cuttings removal
  4. Settling Pits Ineffective
    • Solution: Clean pits
    • Add settling time/area
    • Use screens if available

Good Returns Checklist:

  • Volume in ‚âà Volume out
  • Minimal cuttings (fine chips, not chunks)
  • Clear to slightly cloudy
  • Consistent flow
  • No excessive foam or gas

‚öôÔ∏è Equipment Problems

Engine Won't Start

Systematic Diagnosis:

Check 1: Fuel System

  • Is there fuel in tank?
  • Fuel shut-off valve open?
  • Fuel filter clean?
  • Any air in fuel lines? (Diesel)
  • Fuel quality good? (Not water/debris)

Action: Fill tank, open valve, replace filter, bleed air, drain contaminated fuel

Check 2: Electrical System

  • Battery charged? (Check voltage)
  • Battery terminals clean and tight?
  • Starter engaging?
  • Any blown fuses?

Action: Charge/replace battery, clean terminals, check starter, replace fuses

Check 3: Engine Condition

  • Engine seized? (Try to turn by hand)
  • Oil level adequate?
  • Air filter clean?
  • Safety switches engaged properly?

Action: Free engine if stuck, add oil, clean/replace air filter, check all switches

Check 4: Cold Weather Issues

If temperature below 0¬∞C (32¬∞F):

  • Use engine block heater if available
  • Glow plugs working? (Diesel)
  • Use starting fluid sparingly (CAUTION)
  • Warm engine compartment if possible

Engine Overheating

STOP ENGINE IMMEDIATELY if temperature gauge in red zone

Continued operation can cause catastrophic engine damage

Common Causes & Solutions:

  1. Low Coolant
    • Check coolant level (when cool!)
    • Add 50/50 coolant/water mix
    • Look for leaks if repeatedly low
  2. Radiator Blocked
    • Clean external fins (dust/debris)
    • Check for internal blockage
    • May need professional flush
  3. Thermostat Stuck
    • Replace thermostat
    • Test in hot water to verify operation
  4. Water Pump Failed
    • Check for coolant circulation
    • Look for leaks at pump
    • Replace if faulty
  5. Fan Belt Loose/Broken
    • Check belt tension
    • Look for cracks/damage
    • Replace if needed
  6. Overloaded Engine
    • Reduce drilling parameters
    • Check for mechanical binding
    • May be underpowered for application

Prevention:

  • Check coolant daily
  • Clean radiator weekly
  • Monitor temperature gauge constantly
  • Service cooling system per schedule

Hydraulic System Problems

Low Hydraulic Pressure:

Possible Causes:

  1. Low fluid level
    • Check reservoir
    • Look for leaks
    • Add proper hydraulic oil
  2. Pump worn out
  3. Internal wear reduces pressure
  4. May need rebuild or replacement
  5. Relief valve set too low
    • Adjust to proper pressure
    • Check manual for specs
  6. Filter restricted
    • Replace hydraulic filter
    • Check for contamination

Hydraulic Leaks:

SAFETY WARNING: Hydraulic fluid under pressure can penetrate skin causing serious injury. Never use hands to check for leaks!

Finding Leaks:

  • Use cardboard to locate spray
  • Check all hose connections
  • Inspect cylinder seals
  • Look under equipment for drips

Repairs:

  • Tighten loose fittings
  • Replace damaged hoses
  • Replace worn seals
  • Clean area after repair

Sluggish Movement:

  • Cold fluid: Warm up system before operating
  • Wrong fluid: Use proper viscosity
  • Air in system: Bleed air from cylinders
  • Contaminated fluid: Change fluid, clean system

Pump Problems

No Pressure:

  1. Pump not primed
    • Fill pump with fluid
    • Bleed air from suction line
  2. Suction line blocked
    • Clean strainer/filter
    • Check for collapsed hose
  3. Worn valves or pistons
    • Rebuild or replace pump
  4. Drive coupling broken
    • Inspect and replace coupling

Cavitation (Noisy, Rough Running):

Symptoms: Loud chattering, vibration, pressure fluctuation

Causes & Solutions:

  • Low suction pressure: Raise fluid tank or lower pump
  • Insufficient fluid: Add fluid to tank
  • Blocked suction: Clean suction line and strainer
  • Fluid too viscous: Warm up or use thinner fluid
  • Air leak on suction: Fix all suction line leaks

Preventive Maintenance:

  • Check fluid level daily
  • Clean strainers weekly
  • Replace filters per schedule
  • Inspect hoses regularly
  • Keep fluid clean (no debris)
  • Document pump hours/cycles

üîç Quick Diagnostic Reference Table

Symptom Most Likely Cause Quick Test Fix
Nothing when key turned Dead battery or bad connection Check voltage, wiggle cables Jump start or clean terminals
Click click click Weak battery or bad starter Test battery voltage Charge/replace battery
Cranks but won't fire No fuel or no spark Check fuel valve, check spark plug Open fuel valve or replace plug
Starts then dies Fuel starvation or choke issue Check fuel flow, check choke Clean fuel system, adjust choke
Hard to start when cold Glow plugs (diesel) or choke (gas) Test glow plugs, check choke operation Replace glow plugs or adjust choke
Cranks very slow Weak battery or bad starter Voltage test under load Charge battery or rebuild starter
Backfires through intake Timing off or intake leak Check ignition timing Adjust timing or fix leak
Smoke from exhaust (diesel) White=water/cold, Black=rich, Blue=oil Observe smoke color Warm up, adjust fuel, or check rings

‚õΩ Underground Gas Safety

‚ö†Ô∏è EXTREME HAZARD WARNING

Gases including methane (CH‚ÇÑ), hydrogen sulfide (H‚ÇÇS), and carbon monoxide (CO) can be IMMEDIATELY FATAL.

You CANNOT rely on your senses - most dangerous concentrations are colorless and odorless.

NEVER assume an area is safe without proper gas detection equipment.

METHANE (CH‚ÇÑ) - The Silent Killer

Properties:

  • Colorless, odorless gas
  • Lighter than air (rises to ceiling)
  • Highly flammable and explosive
  • Found in coal seams, organic formations

Explosion Limits:

Concentration Danger Level
5% (LEL) Lower Explosive Limit - DANGER BEGINS
9.5% Most Explosive Concentration
15% (UEL) Upper Explosive Limit

At 5% methane or above:

EVACUATE IMMEDIATELY

  • Any ignition source = EXPLOSION
  • Move to fresh air upwind
  • No smoking, no sparks, no electrical
  • Notify all personnel
  • Do not re-enter until cleared

If Drilling Hits Gas:

  1. STOP advancing immediately
  2. Keep circulating (flush gas out)
  3. Increase ventilation
  4. Monitor continuously
  5. Evacuate if >1%
  6. Consider sealing hole if continues

HYDROGEN SULFIDE (H‚ÇÇS) - Instant Death Gas

‚ö†Ô∏è DEADLIEST GAS - One breath at 700ppm = DEATH

H‚ÇÇS is MORE DANGEROUS than methane. It paralyzes your sense of smell, then kills you.

Properties:

  • Rotten egg smell at LOW concentrations
  • ODORLESS at dangerous levels (smell paralyzed!)
  • Heavier than air (accumulates in low areas)
  • Found in petroleum, sulfur deposits, organic decay

Exposure Effects:

PPM Effect Action
0.1-10 Eye irritation Evacuate area
50-100 Smell gone (paralyzed) EXTREME DANGER
100-200 Respiratory damage Life threatening
500-700 Unconscious immediately FATAL
>700 Instant death One breath kills

If H‚ÇÇS Detected Above 10ppm:

  1. EVACUATE IMMEDIATELY - upwind
  2. DO NOT attempt rescue without SCBA
  3. Call emergency services
  4. Shut down all ignition sources
  5. Do not re-enter - wait for specialists

CARBON MONOXIDE (CO) - The Hidden Killer

Properties:

  • Completely colorless, odorless, tasteless
  • Same weight as air (mixes evenly)
  • Produced by incomplete combustion
  • Binds to blood 200x better than oxygen

Common Sources in Drilling:

  • Diesel engine exhaust
  • Gasoline engines
  • Heaters and generators
  • Any combustion in enclosed space

Exposure Limits:

PPM Effect
35 OSHA 8-hour limit
200 Headache in 2-3 hours
400 Headache in 1 hour
800 Unconscious in 2 hours
1600 Death in 1 hour
12,800 Death in 1-3 minutes

Gas Detection & Monitoring

Required Equipment:

4-Gas Monitor (Minimum):

  • O‚ÇÇ (Oxygen)
  • LEL (Lower Explosive Limit - methane)
  • H‚ÇÇS (Hydrogen Sulfide)
  • CO (Carbon Monoxide)

Alarm Settings (Standard):

Gas Low Alarm High Alarm
O‚ÇÇ 19.5% 23.5%
LEL 10% 20%
H‚ÇÇS 10 ppm 15 ppm
CO 35 ppm 50 ppm

Gas Monitor Procedures:

  • Calibrate before each shift
  • Bump test daily (verify alarm works)
  • Test atmosphere before entering area
  • Test high points (methane rises)
  • Test low points (H‚ÇÇS and CO settle)
  • Never ignore alarms
  • Replace sensors per schedule
  • Keep monitor on your person

If Monitor Alarms:

  1. STOP all work immediately
  2. EVACUATE to fresh air
  3. Account for all personnel
  4. DO NOT re-enter until tested safe
  5. Identify and eliminate source
  6. Increase ventilation
  7. Document incident

Ventilation Requirements

Minimum Standards:

  • Continuous fresh air supply
  • 100 CFM per person minimum
  • Positive pressure system preferred
  • Exhaust gases away from work area
  • Monitor air quality continuously

Warning Signs of Poor Ventilation:

  • Headaches or dizziness
  • Excessive engine exhaust smell
  • Difficulty breathing
  • Fatigue or confusion
  • Eye or throat irritation

‚ö†Ô∏è WHMIS 2015 - Workplace Hazardous Materials Information System

What is WHMIS?

WHMIS 2015 is Canada's hazard communication standard, aligned with the Globally Harmonized System (GHS). It requires:

  • Proper labeling of hazardous products
  • Safety Data Sheets (SDS) available for all hazardous products
  • Worker education and training

WHMIS 2015 vs. Old WHMIS

What Changed:

  • New pictograms (symbols) with red diamond border
  • Standardized signal words: "Danger" or "Warning"
  • 16-section Safety Data Sheets (SDS) instead of 9-section MSDS
  • More specific hazard and precautionary statements
  • Aligned with international GHS standards

WHMIS 2015 Pictograms

üí• Exploding Bomb - Explosive

Hazard Class: Explosive

What it means: Product may explode if heated, dropped, or exposed to flame/spark

Examples: Ammonium nitrate, dynamite, fireworks, ammunition, blasting agents

Safety Precautions:

  • Keep away from heat, sparks, open flames, hot surfaces
  • No smoking near these materials
  • Ground and bond containers when transferring
  • Store in cool, well-ventilated area away from incompatibles
  • Use non-sparking tools
  • Avoid shock, friction, and static discharge

Required PPE:

  • Safety glasses with side shields
  • Fire-resistant clothing
  • Grounding equipment
  • Blast shields where appropriate

üî• Flame - Flammable

Hazard Class: Flammable liquids, gases, aerosols, solids

What it means: Catches fire easily at normal temperatures

Examples: Gasoline, diesel fuel, acetone, propane, alcohol, paint thinner, aerosol sprays

Safety Precautions:

  • Keep away from heat, sparks, flames, and hot surfaces
  • No smoking - enforce strictly
  • Ground and bond containers during transfer
  • Use explosion-proof electrical equipment
  • Store in approved flammable storage cabinets
  • Keep containers tightly closed
  • Use only outdoors or in well-ventilated areas

Required PPE:

  • Safety glasses
  • Chemical-resistant gloves
  • Fire-resistant clothing when handling large quantities
  • Face shield for splash hazard

‚≠ï Flame Over Circle - Oxidizing

Hazard Class: Oxidizing liquids, solids, gases

What it means: Causes or intensifies fire; makes other materials burn more fiercely

Examples: Oxygen, hydrogen peroxide, chlorine, nitric acid, pool chemicals (calcium hypochlorite)

Safety Precautions:

  • Keep away from heat and sources of ignition
  • Store separately from flammable and combustible materials
  • Keep containers tightly closed
  • Do not allow contamination with organics or combustibles
  • Ensure adequate ventilation
  • Clean up spills immediately

Required PPE:

  • Safety glasses or goggles
  • Chemical-resistant gloves
  • Lab coat or protective clothing
  • Face shield for concentrated solutions

üß™ Corrosion - Corrosive to Metals and Skin

Hazard Class: Corrosive to metals, causes severe skin burns and eye damage

What it means: Eats through metal and burns skin/eyes on contact

Examples: Sulfuric acid, hydrochloric acid, caustic soda (sodium hydroxide), battery acid, drain cleaners

Safety Precautions:

  • Wear face shield, chemical-resistant gloves, and apron
  • Do not breathe mist, vapors, or spray
  • Store in corrosion-resistant containers with resistant inner liner
  • Have eyewash station and safety shower immediately available
  • Flush skin immediately if contact occurs (15+ minutes)
  • Never add water to acid - always add acid to water slowly
  • Neutralize spills before cleanup

Required PPE:

  • Chemical splash goggles or face shield
  • Acid/alkali resistant gloves (nitrile, neoprene)
  • Chemical-resistant apron
  • Boots if floor contact possible
  • Respiratory protection if vapors present

üíÄ Skull & Crossbones - Acute Toxicity

Hazard Class: Acute toxicity (fatal or toxic)

What it means: Can cause death or serious harm if swallowed, inhaled, or absorbed through skin

Examples: Pesticides, cyanide compounds, arsenic, some solvents, concentrated ammonia

Safety Precautions:

  • Do NOT eat, drink, or smoke when using these products
  • Avoid breathing dust, fumes, gas, mist, vapors, or spray
  • Use only in well-ventilated area or outdoors
  • Wear appropriate respiratory protection
  • Wash hands and exposed skin thoroughly after handling
  • Store locked up and away from food/feed
  • Have emergency procedures and antidotes ready

Required PPE:

  • Chemical-resistant gloves (check SDS for type)
  • Safety goggles or face shield
  • Respirator (type specified in SDS)
  • Full protective clothing
  • Work in ventilated enclosure if possible

‚ö†Ô∏è Exclamation Mark - Health Hazard (Less Serious)

Hazard Class: Irritant, skin sensitizer, acute toxicity (harmful), narcotic effects

What it means: May cause irritation, allergic skin reaction, drowsiness, or dizziness

Examples: Cleaning products, some paints, adhesives, degreasers, mild acids/bases

Safety Precautions:

  • Avoid prolonged or repeated exposure
  • Use in well-ventilated area
  • Wear gloves if skin contact is possible
  • Follow all label instructions carefully
  • Wash hands after use
  • Keep out of reach of children
  • Do not eat, drink, or smoke while using

Required PPE:

  • Safety glasses
  • Chemical-resistant gloves (if skin contact likely)
  • Protective clothing as needed
  • Adequate ventilation (may need respirator for prolonged use)

‚ò£Ô∏è Health Hazard - Serious Health Effects

Hazard Class: Carcinogen, respiratory sensitizer, reproductive toxicity, organ toxicity, aspiration hazard

What it means: May cause cancer, birth defects, organ damage, respiratory sensitization, or death if swallowed and enters airways

Examples: Asbestos, benzene, formaldehyde, silica dust, chromium compounds, lead

Safety Precautions:

  • Obtain special training before use - DO NOT use without training
  • Minimize exposure - use engineering controls
  • Use appropriate respiratory protection (often required)
  • Ensure proper ventilation - may need enclosed system
  • Follow all safety procedures strictly - no shortcuts
  • Medical surveillance may be required
  • Do not eat, drink, or smoke in work area
  • Shower and change clothes after work shift

Required PPE:

  • Respiratory protection (specified in SDS) - often REQUIRED
  • Chemical-resistant gloves
  • Full protective clothing
  • Safety goggles or face shield
  • Work in controlled environment when possible

üåä Environment - Aquatic Toxicity

Hazard Class: Hazardous to aquatic environment

What it means: Harmful or very toxic to aquatic life, may cause long-term environmental damage

Examples: Pesticides, petroleum products, some cleaning products, heavy metals, certain solvents

Safety Precautions:

  • Prevent release into environment at all costs
  • Do NOT dump down drain, into ground, or into water
  • Dispose only as hazardous waste through approved facility
  • Contain spills immediately - use absorbent materials
  • Follow local, provincial, and federal disposal regulations
  • Report any environmental releases immediately
  • Store in secondary containment

Spill Response:

  • Stop leak if safe to do so
  • Contain with absorbent material
  • Prevent entry into waterways, sewers, or soil
  • Collect and dispose as hazardous waste
  • Report spills as required by law

üßØ Gas Cylinder - Compressed Gas

Hazard Class: Gases under pressure

What it means: Contains gas under pressure; may explode if heated; refrigerated gas may cause cryogenic burns

Examples: Propane, oxygen, nitrogen, acetylene, CO2, helium, compressed air cylinders

Safety Precautions:

  • Protect cylinders from sunlight and temperatures above 50¬∞C (122¬∞F)
  • Secure cylinders upright with chain or strap
  • Do not drop, drag, or roll cylinders
  • Use appropriate regulator for gas type
  • Store in well-ventilated area
  • Keep valve protection cap on when not in use
  • Never use cylinder with damaged valve
  • Open valves slowly
  • Store full and empty cylinders separately

Required PPE:

  • Safety glasses
  • Steel-toed boots
  • Gloves for handling
  • For cryogenic gases: face shield, insulated gloves, protective clothing

How to Read a Safety Data Sheet (SDS)

Every hazardous product must have a 16-section SDS. The SDS provides detailed information about hazards and safe handling.

Section Information Provided
1. Identification Product name, recommended use, supplier contact information
2. Hazard Identification Pictograms, signal words, hazard statements, precautionary statements
3. Composition Chemical ingredients and concentrations
4. First Aid Emergency treatment for exposure
5. Fire-Fighting Suitable extinguishing media, special hazards
6. Accidental Release Spill cleanup procedures and containment
7. Handling & Storage Safe handling practices, storage conditions
8. Exposure Controls/PPE Exposure limits, engineering controls, required PPE
9. Physical/Chemical Properties Appearance, odor, pH, flash point, etc.
10. Stability & Reactivity Chemical stability, incompatible materials
11. Toxicological Information Health effects from exposure
12. Ecological Information Environmental effects
13. Disposal Proper disposal methods
14. Transport Information Shipping classifications and requirements
15. Regulatory Information Applicable regulations
16. Other Information Date of preparation, revision history

Most Important SDS Sections for Workers:

  • Section 2: Know the hazards!
  • Section 4: First aid - critical in emergency
  • Section 7: How to handle safely
  • Section 8: What PPE you need

Common Drilling Chemicals & Their Hazards

Chemical/Product Pictograms Main Hazards Key Precautions
Diesel Fuel üî• ‚ö†Ô∏è Flammable, skin irritant, aspiration hazard Ground containers, avoid skin contact, no smoking
Gasoline üî• ‚ö†Ô∏è ‚ò£Ô∏è Highly flammable, toxic, carcinogenic No sparks/flames, use outdoors, avoid breathing vapors
Hydraulic Oil ‚ö†Ô∏è Skin/eye irritant Wear gloves, avoid prolonged skin contact
Bentonite (Dry) ‚ö†Ô∏è Respiratory irritant Avoid breathing dust, use in ventilated area
Propane/LPG üî• üßØ Extremely flammable gas, asphyxiant Use outdoors, check for leaks, no flames
Battery Acid (Sulfuric) üß™ Severe burns to skin/eyes, corrosive Face shield, acid gloves, eyewash nearby
Antifreeze (Ethylene Glycol) ‚ö†Ô∏è üåä Toxic if swallowed, environmental hazard Don't ingest, proper disposal required
Degreasers/Solvents üî• ‚ö†Ô∏è Flammable, skin irritant, narcotic Ventilation, avoid breathing, wear gloves
Concrete/Cement (Wet) üß™ ‚ö†Ô∏è Skin burns (alkaline), eye damage Waterproof gloves, eye protection, wash immediately

Emergency Response by Hazard Class

üî• Fire (Flammable Materials):

  • Evacuate if fire is large
  • Use appropriate extinguisher (ABC for most, CO2 for electrical)
  • Never use water on flammable liquid fires
  • Shut off fuel source if safe to do so
  • Cool nearby containers with water spray

üß™ Chemical Burns (Corrosives):

  • Flush affected area with water for 15-20 minutes minimum
  • Remove contaminated clothing while flushing
  • Do NOT try to neutralize on skin
  • Get medical attention immediately
  • For eyes: continuous flushing, get to hospital

üíÄ Poisoning (Toxic Materials):

  • Remove person from exposure immediately
  • Call Poison Control: 1-800-268-9017 (Canada)
  • Have SDS available when you call
  • Do NOT induce vomiting unless instructed
  • Monitor breathing and consciousness
  • Get medical attention immediately

üåä Environmental Spill:

  • Stop leak if safe to do so
  • Contain spill - prevent entry to water/sewers
  • Absorb with appropriate materials
  • Dispose as hazardous waste
  • Report spills as required by regulation
  • Clean contaminated area thoroughly

‚ö†Ô∏è WHMIS 2025 - Major Updates Effective December 2024

Canada is adopting the 8th Revised Edition of the Globally Harmonized System (GHS Rev. 8), bringing significant changes to workplace hazard communication. These updates become mandatory in December 2024.

üóìÔ∏è Implementation Timeline:

  • December 15, 2024: WHMIS 2025 regulations come into force
  • December 15, 2025: Manufacturers/importers must comply with new SDS and label requirements
  • December 15, 2026: Distributors must comply (1-year transition)
  • December 15, 2027: Employers must update workplace labels and worker training (3-year transition)

üÜï New Hazard Classes Added in WHMIS 2025

WHMIS 2025 introduces three completely new hazard classes that were not in WHMIS 2015.

New Hazard Class Description Why It Matters
Desensitized Explosives Explosive substances that have been desensitized (made less sensitive) by adding water or other substances Common in construction, mining explosives that are transported/stored more safely
Pyrophoric Gases Gases that can ignite spontaneously in air at or below 54¬∞C (129¬∞F) Specialized industrial applications, spontaneous ignition risk
Non-Flammable Aerosols (Category 3) Aerosol products that don't meet flammability criteria but still contain compressed gas Previously unclassified aerosols now require proper labeling

Drilling Industry Impact: Desensitized explosives classification affects blasting operations. Pyrophoric gases may be encountered in specialized drilling fluids or gas analysis equipment.

üîÑ Modified Hazard Classes in WHMIS 2025

Several existing hazard classes have been updated with revised criteria or additional categories.

Flammable Gases - New Category Added:

Category WHMIS 2015 WHMIS 2025
Category 1A Did not exist NEW: Extremely flammable gases (most severe)
Category 1B Was "Category 1" Flammable gases (renamed from Category 1)
Category 2 Chemically unstable gases No change - still chemically unstable gases

Skin Corrosion/Irritation - Revised Criteria:

Change Impact
Updated testing protocols Some products may be reclassified based on new test methods
Refined category definitions More precise classification of corrosive vs irritant substances

Aspiration Hazard - Clarified Criteria:

  • Refined kinematic viscosity measurements
  • Updated guidance on hydrocarbon mixtures
  • Clearer classification of petroleum products

Drilling Products Affected: Hydraulic fluids, diesel fuel, lubricants, and solvents may have updated classifications under revised aspiration hazard criteria.

üè∑Ô∏è New Pictogram: Desensitized Explosives

WHMIS 2025 introduces one new pictogram for desensitized explosives.

Pictogram Description Used For
üí• Exploding Bomb (with bar) Exploding bomb symbol with horizontal bar underneath (differentiates from regular explosives) Desensitized explosives only

All WHMIS 2025 Pictograms (Complete Set):

Symbol Name Hazards
üí• Exploding Bomb Explosives, Self-reactives, Organic peroxides
üî• Flame Flammables, Self-reactives, Pyrophorics, Self-heating, Organic peroxides
‚≠ïüî• Flame Over Circle Oxidizers
üõ¢Ô∏è Gas Cylinder Gases under pressure
‚ò†Ô∏è Skull & Crossbones Acute toxicity (fatal or toxic)
üß™‚öóÔ∏è Corrosion Skin corrosion/burns, Eye damage, Corrosive to metals
‚ùó Exclamation Mark Irritant, Skin sensitizer, Acute toxicity (harmful), Narcotic effects, STOT-SE
‚öïÔ∏è Health Hazard Respiratory sensitizer, Mutagen, Carcinogen, Reproductive toxicity, STOT-SE/RE, Aspiration hazard
üåç Environment Aquatic toxicity (NOTE: Not required on WHMIS labels but may appear on GHS labels)
üí•‚ûñ Exploding Bomb with Bar NEW in 2025: Desensitized explosives

Important: The biohazardous infectious materials pictogram remains separate from GHS pictograms and continues to be used under WHMIS for biohazardous materials.

üìÑ Safety Data Sheet (SDS) Changes

WHMIS 2025 updates multiple sections of the 16-section SDS format with new information requirements.

Major SDS Section Updates:

Section What's New in WHMIS 2025
Section 2:
Hazard Identification		 ‚Ä¢ Must include new hazard classes (desensitized explosives, pyrophoric gases)
‚Ä¢ Updated signal words and hazard statements for modified classes
‚Ä¢ New precautionary statements
Section 3:
Composition/Information on Ingredients		 ‚Ä¢ Updated disclosure requirements
‚Ä¢ Revised concentration ranges
‚Ä¢ Clearer guidance on trade secrets vs. required disclosure
Section 9:
Physical & Chemical Properties		 ‚Ä¢ Additional properties may be required
‚Ä¢ Updated test methods for particle size distribution
‚Ä¢ New parameters for nanomaterials
Section 11:
Toxicological Information		 ‚Ä¢ Revised criteria for acute toxicity estimates
‚Ä¢ Updated skin corrosion/irritation testing guidance
‚Ä¢ New aspiration hazard classification criteria
Section 12:
Ecological Information		 ‚Ä¢ Enhanced aquatic toxicity information
‚Ä¢ Updated persistence and bioaccumulation data
‚Ä¢ NOTE: Still not mandatory for WHMIS compliance but often included

Action Required: Employers must obtain updated SDSs from suppliers by December 2025 and update workplace training by December 2027.

üè∑Ô∏è Label Updates in WHMIS 2025

Supplier and workplace labels must be updated to reflect new hazard classifications and pictograms.

Supplier Label Changes:

Label Element WHMIS 2025 Requirement
Product Identifier No change - must match SDS
Pictograms Must include new desensitized explosives pictogram where applicable
Signal Word Updated signal words for revised hazard classes
Hazard Statements New statements for new hazard classes, updated statements for revised classes
Precautionary Statements Revised and expanded precautionary statements to match GHS Rev. 8
Supplier Identifier No change

Workplace Label Requirements:

  • Must include updated product identifier matching new SDS
  • Safe handling information must reflect new hazard classifications
  • Reference to updated SDS must be included
  • Employers have until December 2027 to update existing workplace labels

Transition Period Flexibility: During transition (2024-2027), both WHMIS 2015 and WHMIS 2025 labels may be in circulation. Always refer to the most recent SDS available.

üë∑ Worker Training Requirements for WHMIS 2025

Employers must update worker training to include all WHMIS 2025 changes by December 15, 2027.

Required Training Updates:

Training Topic What Workers Must Learn
New Hazard Classes ‚Ä¢ What desensitized explosives are
‚Ä¢ What pyrophoric gases are
‚Ä¢ Non-flammable aerosol hazards
‚Ä¢ How to identify products in these classes
Modified Classifications ‚Ä¢ Changes to flammable gas categories
‚Ä¢ Updated skin corrosion/irritation criteria
‚Ä¢ Revised aspiration hazard classifications
New Pictogram ‚Ä¢ Recognize desensitized explosives pictogram
‚Ä¢ Understand difference from regular explosives pictogram
‚Ä¢ Know appropriate handling procedures
Updated SDSs ‚Ä¢ How to find new information in revised SDSs
‚Ä¢ Changes to specific sections
‚Ä¢ Where to access updated SDSs
Label Changes ‚Ä¢ Identify updated supplier labels
‚Ä¢ Recognize new hazard statements
‚Ä¢ Understand new precautionary statements

Training Timeline for Employers:

  • Now - December 2025: Begin familiarizing supervisors with WHMIS 2025 changes
  • 2025-2026: Develop updated training materials and programs
  • 2026-2027: Deliver updated training to all workers who handle hazardous products
  • By December 15, 2027: All workers must complete WHMIS 2025 training
  • Ongoing: Train new hires on WHMIS 2025 from the start

Best Practice: Don't wait until 2027! Start updating training programs now. Early adoption reduces confusion during the transition period and ensures worker safety.

üîß WHMIS 2025 Impact on Drilling Operations

Specific implications for mineral exploration and drilling worksites.

Common Drilling Products Affected:

Product Type Potential Changes Action Required
Diesel Fuel May be reclassified under revised aspiration hazard criteria Obtain updated SDS, review handling procedures
Hydraulic Fluids Classification may change based on updated skin irritation criteria Check for new pictograms, update workplace labels
Drilling Lubricants Aspiration hazard classification may be updated Review PPE requirements, update training
Aerosol Products Non-flammable aerosols now classified (Category 3) Previously unlabeled aerosols may now require WHMIS labels
Blasting Agents May fall under desensitized explosives classification New pictogram, updated handling procedures
Compressed Gases Pyrophoric gas category added (specialized applications) Verify classification, ensure proper storage
Solvents & Degreasers Flammable gas subcategories may affect classification Review fire safety procedures

Worksite Compliance Checklist:

  • Inventory all hazardous products currently on site
  • Contact suppliers to obtain WHMIS 2025 compliant SDSs
  • Review each SDS for classification changes
  • Update workplace labels where products have changed
  • Revise safe work procedures for reclassified products
  • Update emergency response plans if needed
  • Schedule WHMIS 2025 training for all workers
  • Update WHMIS binders/digital systems with new SDSs
  • Ensure new products purchased come with WHMIS 2025 compliant labels/SDSs

Supervisor Responsibility: Drill supervisors must ensure all hazardous products on site have current WHMIS 2025 compliant SDSs and that workers are trained on any changes affecting their work.

üìã Key Differences: WHMIS 2015 vs WHMIS 2025

Quick reference comparing the two systems.

Feature WHMIS 2015 (GHS Rev. 5) WHMIS 2025 (GHS Rev. 8)
Number of Hazard Classes 28 classes 31 classes (3 new)
Pictograms 9 pictograms 10 pictograms (1 new)
Flammable Gases Category 1 and Category 2 Category 1A, 1B, and 2
Desensitized Explosives Not included New hazard class
Pyrophoric Gases Not separately classified New hazard class
Aerosols Categories 1 and 2 only Categories 1, 2, and 3 (non-flammable)
Aspiration Hazard Original criteria Refined criteria for hydrocarbons
Skin Corrosion/Irritation Original testing methods Updated protocols
SDS Format 16 sections (GHS Rev. 5) 16 sections (GHS Rev. 8 updated)
Compliance Deadline Fully implemented December 15, 2027 (full compliance)

Bottom Line: WHMIS 2025 doesn't replace WHMIS 2015 - it updates and expands it. Most core principles remain the same, with additions to cover new hazard types and refined classifications for existing hazards.

‚ùì Common Questions About WHMIS 2025

Q: Do I need to throw away all my WHMIS 2015 materials?

A: No. During the transition period (2024-2027), both systems are acceptable. However, start incorporating WHMIS 2025 updates now. By December 2027, all training materials must reflect WHMIS 2025.

Q: What if my supplier hasn't provided updated SDSs yet?

A: Suppliers have until December 15, 2025 to provide WHMIS 2025 compliant SDSs. Contact them to request updated versions. Continue using WHMIS 2015 SDSs in the meantime but plan for updates.

Q: Do workplace labels need to be updated immediately?

A: No. Employers have until December 15, 2027 to update workplace labels. However, if you're creating new workplace labels, consider using WHMIS 2025 format to avoid redoing them later.

Q: Are the pictograms completely different?

A: No. Only ONE new pictogram was added (desensitized explosives with bar). All other pictograms remain the same. Workers familiar with WHMIS 2015 pictograms will recognize WHMIS 2025 pictograms.

Q: How much training is required for WHMIS 2025?

A: Workers who already have WHMIS 2015 training need supplemental training covering the changes (new hazard classes, modified classifications, new pictogram). This doesn't require completely redoing foundational WHMIS training - just updating for the changes.

Q: What if I work with products that aren't affected by the changes?

A: Even if your specific products haven't changed classification, you still need WHMIS 2025 awareness training so you can recognize and understand the new hazard classes and pictograms if you encounter them.

Q: Where can I find official WHMIS 2025 resources?

A: Health Canada and the Canadian Centre for Occupational Health and Safety (CCOHS) provide official guidance documents, training materials, and implementation tools on their websites.

Key Takeaway: WHMIS 2025 is an evolution, not a revolution. The transition period allows time to update systems gradually. Start now to avoid last-minute scrambling in 2027.

üéØ Action Plan for Drilling Companies

Step-by-step implementation guide for drilling operations.

Phase 1: Preparation (Now - Mid 2025)

  • Designate a WHMIS 2025 implementation coordinator
  • Review WHMIS 2025 changes and assess impact on operations
  • Create inventory of all hazardous products currently used
  • Contact suppliers to confirm WHMIS 2025 compliance timelines
  • Begin developing updated training materials

Phase 2: Transition (Mid 2025 - End 2026)

  • Obtain WHMIS 2025 compliant SDSs as they become available
  • Review new SDSs for classification changes
  • Update chemical inventory system with new information
  • Revise site-specific safe work procedures as needed
  • Train supervisors and safety personnel on WHMIS 2025
  • Begin updating workplace labels on long-term containers

Phase 3: Implementation (2026 - December 2027)

  • Deliver WHMIS 2025 training to all workers
  • Complete updating all workplace labels
  • Ensure all new products purchased are WHMIS 2025 compliant
  • Update emergency response plans if needed
  • Conduct compliance audit before December 2027 deadline
  • Document all training and updates for regulatory compliance

Phase 4: Ongoing Compliance (2027+)

  • Train all new hires using WHMIS 2025 curriculum
  • Keep SDS binders/systems current with latest versions
  • Monitor for future WHMIS updates from Health Canada
  • Conduct annual WHMIS refresher training
  • Review and update as new products are introduced

Success Strategy: Don't view WHMIS 2025 as a compliance burden - it's an opportunity to refresh your hazard communication program and ensure worker safety. Companies that start early will have smoother transitions and better-prepared workers.

WHMIS Training Requirements

By Law, employers MUST provide:

  • Education about WHMIS before working with hazardous products
  • Training on specific products used in workplace
  • Training on how to read labels and SDS
  • Training on safe work procedures
  • Training on emergency procedures
  • Retraining when products or procedures change

Workers have the RIGHT to:

  • Know what hazardous products they're working with
  • Access SDS for all products
  • Receive proper training
  • Refuse unsafe work

üî© Rods & Bits Reference

Rod Size Specifications

Series OD (mm) Core √ò (mm) Hole √ò (mm) Max Depth
AQ 48mm 27mm 48mm 300m
BQ 60mm 36.5mm 60mm 600m
NQ 76mm 47.6mm 76mm 1000m
HQ 96mm 63.5mm 96mm 1500m
PQ 123mm 85mm 123mm 2000m

NQ is the industry standard - Best balance of core size, strength, and portability

Bit Types & Selection

Surface-Set Bits:

  • Construction: Diamonds set in surface of bit face
  • Best for: Soft to medium formations
  • Advantages: Aggressive cutting, higher penetration rates
  • Disadvantages: Shorter life in hard/abrasive rock

Impregnated Bits:

  • Construction: Diamonds distributed throughout matrix
  • Best for: Medium to very hard formations
  • Advantages: Long life, consistent performance
  • Disadvantages: Slower penetration, more expensive

Ground Hardness & Bit Selection:

Formation Hardness Recommended Bit
Quartzite, Chert Very Hard/Abrasive Impregnated - Premium Hard Matrix
Granite, Basalt Hard Impregnated - Standard/Premium
Limestone, Dolomite Medium-Hard Impregnated or Surface-Set
Sandstone (cemented) Medium Either type works
Shale, Mudstone Soft Surface-Set
Fault Zones Variable/Broken Impregnated - Tough Matrix

Bit Wear Patterns

Normal Wear:

  • Even diamond exposure
  • Matrix worn evenly
  • Waterways intact
  • Gauge diameter maintained

Abnormal Wear Indicates Problems:

Wear Pattern Cause Solution
Heavy center wear Excessive WOB Reduce weight on bit
Gauge wear Abrasive formation Use harder matrix, add stabilizers
Washed out waterways Excessive pump pressure Reduce pressure
Polished diamonds Insufficient WOB/RPM Increase parameters
Loaded/balled face Poor flushing Improve fluid properties

EXCORE 10 8 - 9 Extremely Hard Jasperite, Quartzite - softer matrix

Fordia Tip: HERO 7 is the most popular matrix in the industry - excellent balance of penetration and lifespan

üíé Boart Longyear Longyear‚Ñ¢ Bit Selection Guide

Color-coded system makes bit selection easy - cuts faster right out of the box and lasts longer.

Longyear‚Ñ¢ Diamond Bit Series

Color Code Mohs Scale Ground Type Typical Formations
üü£ PURPLE 1 - 4.5 Very Soft to Soft Clay, Shale, Soft Sedimentary
üîµ BLUE 4 - 5.5 Soft to Medium Sandstone, Limestone, Dolomite
üü¢ GREEN 5 - 6.5 Medium to Medium-Hard Marble, Schist, Some Granite
üü° YELLOW 5.5 - 7 Medium-Hard to Hard Granite, Gneiss - Faster penetration
üü† ORANGE 6.5 - 7.5 Hard Hard Granite, Basalt
üî¥ RED 7.5 - 9 Very Hard to Extremely Hard Quartzite, Chert, Taconite

Key Features:

  • Razorcut‚Ñ¢ Technology: Diamond protrusions on bit face cut right out of the box, even in soft ground
  • Chemical Diamond Bonding: 80% diamond projection vs 40% mechanical bonding = longer life & faster penetration
  • Tapered Swirl (TSW) Geometry: Fast penetration in competent ground, easily pushes cuttings in broken ground

Bit Selection Tips:

  • Overlapping Ranges: When ground is 6.5 Mohs, choose Green for longer life or Yellow for faster penetration
  • Shallow Holes: Prioritize penetration rate (choose softer matrix) - rod trips are quick
  • Deep Holes: Prioritize bit life (choose harder matrix) - rod trips take longer
  • Use Mohs Scratch Test: Determine exact rock hardness ¬±0.5 for optimal bit selection

Performance Data (Australian Trials):

  • 60% improvement over competition
  • 2x penetration rate increase
  • 23% more core in the box
  • Improved shift performance and meters drilled

‚öñÔ∏è Comparing Fordia vs Boart Longyear

Feature Fordia Boart Longyear
